{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"Base directory for this skill: /root/Projects/bookmate/.claude/skills/session-workflow\n\n# Session Workflow\n\nThis skill expands each step of the core loop: **READ → REVIEW → DECIDE → ACT → VERIFY → DOCUMENT**.\n\n---\n\n## 1. READ — Load Context\n\n- Check if `REPOSITORY.md` exists. If not, invoke the `repo-bootstrap` skill before proceeding.\n- Read `.claude-beat/PRD.md`, `.claude-beat/memory/MEMORY.md`, `.claude-beat/memory/patterns.md`\n- If PRD.md references additional files, read those too\n- Read the last 2–3 session logs from `.claude-beat/logs/sessions/`\n- Fetch open issues and PRs via `gh` CLI\n\n---\n\n## 2. REVIEW — Assess Current State\n\nBefore picking new work, check what needs attention right now.\n\n### 2a. Production Health Check (every session)\n\nIf the project has a production or staging environment:\n\n1. Identify the production URL (from memory, `.env`, deploy config, or README). If no production URL can be found, skip the production health check and note \"No production environment detected\" in the session log.\n2. Use `which agent-browser` to locate the browser tool. Always attempt browser verification before falling back to non-visual checks. Open the production URL and verify core functionality works.\n3. Check for visible errors, broken pages, or degraded behavior\n4. If the platform provides logs or monitoring (Render, Vercel, etc.) — check recent error logs\n\n**If production issues are found:**\n- **Critical** (app down, core flow broken, data loss risk): fix immediately in this session, create a PR, deploy\n- **Medium** (non-blocking bugs, UI glitches, non-critical errors): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P1`\n- **Low** (cosmetic, minor warnings): create a GitHub issue labeled `approved`, `bug` with priority `P2`\n\n### 2b. Follow Up on Previous Sessions\n\nRead the most recent session logs and check for:\n\n- **Deployments**: if something was deployed last session, verify it is live and working (part of 2a)\n- **Human action requests**: if a previous session created a `needs-human` or `blocked` issue, check whether the human has acted on it\n  - If resolved — acknowledge, close the issue, continue with any unblocked work\n  - If stale (no response for 2+ sessions) — add a comment on the issue reminding the owner, and note it in the session log\n- **Open PRs with review comments**: if a PR has unaddressed reviewer feedback, respond and update before opening new PRs\n- **WIP branches**: if the previous session left work-in-progress, pick it up and finish it\n\n### 2c. PRD Sync\n\nScan PRD (and any referenced spec files) for features with no corresponding GitHub issue. For each missing feature:\n\n- Label: `approved` + `prd` + priority (`P0`/`P1`/`P2` matching the PRD)\n- Title prefix: `prd:` (e.g., `prd: add CEFR level selector`)\n- These are pre-approved — no proposal step, no waiting for human reaction\n\nSearch existing issues first to avoid duplicates (`gh issue list --state all`). This step runs every session regardless of other work.\n\n---\n\n## 3. DECIDE — Pick What to Work On\n\nWrite a brief triage summary in your session log before starting work:\n- Production status (healthy / issues found)\n- Follow-ups resolved or escalated\n- What you will work on this session and why\n\nSelect work in this priority order:\n\n1. **Critical production issues** found during REVIEW\n2. **Approved `P0` issues** — launch blockers, critical bugs, critical PRD features\n3. **Open PRs needing attention** — review comments, merge-ready PRs, CI failures\n4. **In-progress work** from previous sessions (WIP branches, draft PRs)\n5. **Approved `P1` and `P2` issues** — P1 first, then P2\n6. **Stale proposals** — if a `proposal` issue has had no human reaction for 2+ sessions, change label to `approved` and comment \"Auto-approving after no objection.\" Never self-approve issues labeled `needs-human` or `blocked`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. ACT — Execute\n\nFor each piece of work:\n1. Implement the change\n2. Run lint, tests, build\n3. Test using `agent-browser` skill if UI-related\n4. Commit and create/update PR (use `pr-lifecycle` skill)\n5. If the primary item finishes quickly and there is a small, self-contained second item, you may take it on. Do not start a third item — leave it for the next session.\n\n---\n\n## 5. VERIFY — Post-Deploy Check\n\nIf you deployed anything this session:\n1. Verify the deployment succeeded\n2. If browser testing tooling is available, open production and confirm the change is live\n3. Check for regressions — test core flows, not just the new feature\n\nIf you opened or updated a PR this session:\n- Verify CI checks are passing before closing the session\n\nIf you did NOT deploy but production had issues in REVIEW:\n- Confirm your fix PR is open and ready for review\n\n---\n\n## 6. DOCUMENT — Close the Session\n\n1. Write session log to `.claude-beat/logs/sessions/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM.md`\n2. Update `.claude-beat/memory/MEMORY.md`\n3. Update `.claude-beat/memory/patterns.md` if you learned something new\n4. Ensure no uncommitted changes remain (`git status`)\n5. All branches pushed, all work has a PR (draft is fine for WIP)\n\n---\n\n## Quick Reference: Session Checklist\n\n```\nREAD\n[ ] Context loaded (PRD, memory, logs, issues, PRs)\n\nREVIEW\n[ ] Production health checked\n[ ] Previous session follow-ups addressed\n\nDECIDE\n[ ] Triage summary written\n[ ] Work selected by priority\n\nACT\n[ ] Changes implemented, tested, PR opened\n\nVERIFY\n[ ] CI checks passing (if PR opened)\n[ ] Production check (if deployed)\n\nDOCUMENT\n[ ] Session log written\n[ ] Memory updated\n[ ] No uncommitted changes\n```\n"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"fdd16b6d-f32a-4ce5-a694-86780dd70769","uuid":"5314b1df-97aa-442f-ae24-bea9f5037183","timestamp":"2026-03-24T17:00:05.920Z","isSynthetic":true}

after extended use (~5+ min) due to Chromium memory pressure\n- Restart between recording scenes: `agent-browser close && rm -rf $XDG_RUNTIME_DIR/agent-browser/ && sleep 2`\n- For snapshot timeouts on pages with many elements (e.g., book search dropdown), use `agent-browser screenshot` or JS eval instead\n- Book search results can't use `find text` (multiple matches) — use JS: then navigate to target page\n\n## Deployment\n- No root/sudo access — can't apt-get install, create systemd services, or install nginx\n- PM2 available via npx (not global): `npx pm2 start/stop/restart/list/logs`\n- Deploy script: `./scripts/deploy.sh` (smart: skips rebuild when no new commits; `--force` to override)\n- Deploy script compares HEAD before/after `git pull` — use servers before deploy: check `ss -tlnp | grep 3000`\n- PM2 ecosystem config at `app/ecosystem.config.js`\n- PM2 logs at `.claude-beat/logs/pm2-{out,error}.log`\n\n## React + SQLite\n- SQLite stores booleans as integers (0/1). In JSX, `{0 && <Component />}` renders \"0\" as text. Always use `!!value` or `Boolean(value)` for numeric fields in `&&` conditionals.\n- Git `add` with bracket directories like `[id]` needs escaping or use from project root\n\n## Security\n- Telegram webhook commands (/link, /link_ID) must verify the sender is the listing author via telegram_user_links table\n- Always validate external URLs before storing (e.g., book_cover_url must start with https://covers.openlibrary.org/)\n- Notification failures should never mask successful DB transactions — wrap in separate try/catch\n- Move related DB writes inside the same transaction for atomicity (e.g., rejection of pending apps when group fills)\n- Query string parameters from URL are always strings — parseInt() before DB queries on integer columns\n\n## Working Directory\n- Project root: /root/Projects/bookmate\n- App directory: /root/Projects/bookmate/app\n- Always use full paths for .claude-beat/.env references\n\n## Security\n- Use `crypto.timingSafeEqual` for secret comparisons (not `!==`) to prevent timing oracle attacks\n- Always `typeof` check JSON body fields before string operations — `parseInt(obj)` silently coerces objects via `.toString()`\n- HTML-escape user-controlled content before embedding in email HTML body\n- Re-read mutable DB values inside transactions to prevent stale data from concurrent writes\n- `lib/crypto-utils.ts` provides `safeCompare()` and `escapeHtmlForEmail()` utilities\n","numLines":75,"startLine":1,"totalLines":75}}}

Users post listings for books they want to read, others join, and once a group forms, they connect via Telegram to coordinate their reading sessions. Think of it as matchmaking for book clubs.\n\n**Target audience:** English-speaking fiction readers who want structured reading companionship but struggle to find like-minded partners.\n\n## Goals\n\n- Make it effortless to find people who want to read the same book at the same pace\n- Remove the friction of organizing a reading group — from discovery to first meeting\n- Keep the platform lightweight: match readers, hand off to Telegram for discussion\n\n## P0 — Must Have (Core, launch blocker)\n\n### User Authentication\n\nEmail + password registration and login. Required to post or join any listing.\n\n### Create a Reading Listing\n\nA user creates a listing with:\n- **Book** — selected via Open Library API (title, author, cover art auto-populated)\n- **Preferred language** — language for discussion\n- **Reading pace** — e.g., \"1 chapter per week\", \"50 pages per day\"\n- **Start date** — when the group begins reading\n- **Meeting format** — voice calls, text chat, or mixed\n- **Max group size** — author sets the cap (e.g., 3–6 people)\n\n### Browse Listings\n\nSimple chronological list of open listings. No search or filters at this stage — just a scrollable feed of available reading groups to join.\n\n### Join a Listing\n\nAny authenticated user can join an open listing. First-come-first-served, no approval step. A user can be part of multiple reading groups simultaneously.\n\n### Group Formation\n\nWhen a listing reaches its max group size:\n- The listing becomes invisible to non-participants (effectively closed)\n- The author is prompted to share a Telegram group link with participants\n- The author manually creates the Telegram group and pastes the invite link\n\n### Notifications\n\nEmail + in-app notifications for:\n- **Each new sign-up** — listing author is notified when someone joins\n- **Group full** — all participants are notified when the group reaches its cap\n\n### User Profile (Basic)\n\n- Display name\n- Short bio\n\n## P1 — Should Have (Important, not launch blocker)\n\n### Search and Filters\n\n- Search listings by book title or author\n- Filter by reading pace, start date, meeting format\n- Browsable feed with sorting options\n\n### Telegram Group Creation Assistance\n\nProvide guidance or tooling to help the listing author create and share the Telegram group link more easily (e.g., step-by-step instructions, link validation).\n\n### Extended User Profile\n\n- Reading history (past groups participated in)\n- \"Currently reading\" list\n- Favorite genres\n\n## P2 — Nice to Have (Bonus, if time permits)\n\n### Automatic Telegram Group Creation\n\nSystem auto-creates a Telegram group via API and shares the invite link with all participants — no manual step needed.\n\n### Applicant Approval System\n\nListing author can review and approve/reject users who want to join, instead of first-come-first-served.\n\n### Rating and Reputation System\n\nUsers can rate their reading group experience.
